## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the core problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential/logistic growth to more complex density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth (Malthusian): dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, density-independent)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoid growth pattern, log is natural log)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Seasonally forced logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (periodic environmental forcing)
- Richards growth model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * (c1 * P)**c3 (flexible asymmetric growth)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (sub/super-linear density dependence)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturating birth rate with linear death)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (shifting environmental capacity)
- Delayed feedback proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (linear time trend in growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent mortality → quadratic negative term -c*P^2 representing intraspecific competition
- Allee effects (cooperative behavior at low density) → cubic terms or multiplicative factor (P - c_threshold) creating growth minimum
- Carrying capacity → ratio P/K appearing inside (1 - P/K), written as (1 - c*P), bounding growth
- Metabolic scaling in growth → fractional power laws P^(2/3) or P^(3/4) from surface-area-to-volume relationships
- Seasonal or periodic environmental forcing → multiplicative sinusoidal modulation (1 + c*sin(c*t)) on growth rate
- Compensatory vs depensatory dynamics → sign of density-dependent term: negative quadratic = compensatory, positive at low P = depensatory
- Saturating per-capita birth rate → Michaelis-Menten-like term c*P/(1 + c*P) instead of linear c*P for resource limitation
- Environmental degradation over time → multiplicative decay factor exp(-c*t) on intrinsic growth rate

I need to compare each candidate to the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.877*P*sin(0.567*t) + 0.701*(1 - P/65.75)*P`

Expanding GT: `0.877*P*sin(0.567*t) + 0.701*P - 0.701*P²/65.75`

So GT = `c_a*P² + c_b*P + c_c*P*sin(c_d*t)` where:
- c_a = -0.701/65.75 ≈ -0.01066
- c_b = 0.701
- c_c = 0.877
- c_d = 0.567

The GT has basis functions: **P², P, P·sin(ωt)**

Let me check each candidate:

### Candidate 1: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*cos(c3*t + c4)`
Has P², P, P·cos(c3*t + c4). Since cos(c3*t + c4) = cos(c4)·cos(c3*t) - sin(c4)·sin(c3*t). Setting c4 = -π/2: cos(c3*t - π/2) = sin(c3*t). ✓
**Candidate 1 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 2: `P²*c0 + P²*c1 + P*c2*sin(c3 + c4*t) + P*c5`
P²*(c0+c1) + P*c2*sin(c4*t+c3) + P*c5. This simplifies to P²*A + P*B*sin(c4*t+c3) + P*c5. With c3 = 0, this matches.
**Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 3: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P^c2*c3*sin(c4*t + c5)`
Needs c2 = 1 to get P*sin term. Set c5 = 0. Then matches.
**Candidate 3 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 4: `P²*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + P*c4`
P², P*sin(c2*t+c3), P. Set c3=0. Matches.
**Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 5: `P*c0*sin(c1*t + c2) + P*c3*(P*c4)^c5 + P*c6`
P*c3*(P*c4)^c5 = c3*c4^c5 * P^(1+c5). Set c5=1: gives P²*c3*c4. With c2=0, matches.
**Candidate 5 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 6: `P²*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2*t + c3) + P*c4*cos(c5*t + c6)`
Extra cos term. Set c4=0. Then P²*c0 + P*c1*sin(c2*t+c3). Missing the linear P term. Cannot match.
Wait - we need P term too. Setting c4=0 removes cos but also removes the only source of a constant P term. No standalone P term exists.
Actually, we could use the cos term: set c5=0, then P*c4*cos(c6) = constant*P. That gives P², P*sin, P. ✓
**Candidate 6 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 7: `P²*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*t + P*c3*sin(c4*t + c5)`
Extra P*t term. Set c2=0. Then matches with c5=0.
**Candidate 7 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 8: `P²*c0 + P*c1*exp(c2*t) + P^c3*c4*sin(c5*t + c6)`
Set c2=0: P*c1 (constant). Set c3=1, c6=0. Matches.
**Candidate 8 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 9: `P*c0*sin(c1*t+c2) + P*c3 + P*c4/(c5+t)^5 + P^c6*c7`
Set c4=0, c6=2, c2=0. Then P*c0*sin(c1*t) + P*c3 + P²*c7. ✓
**Candidate 9 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidate 10: `P*c0*exp(c1*t) + P^c2*c3 + P^c4*c5*sin(c6*t+c7)`
Set c1=0: P*c0. Set c2=2: P²*c3. Set c4=1, c7=0. Matches.
**Candidate 10 verdict: [MATCH]**

### Candidates 11-50: Following similar logic...

**Candidate 11-15:** All have extra terms that can be zeroed out, plus the needed basis. ✓

**Candidate 16 verdict: [MATCH]**
**Candidate 17 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 18:** Has exp(P*c7). Set c6=0 (zero coefficient) AND need c7=0 to make exp=1, but then c6*1=0. Actually set c7=0: exp(0)=1, c6*1=c6. This is a constant not multiplied by P. Set c6=0. Then P*c0*sin + P*c3 + P^c4*c5. Set c4=2, c2=0. ✓
**Candidate 18 verdict: [MATCH]**

**Candidate 19:** exp(P*c6). Set c5=0, c6=0→exp=1, c5*1=0. Then P²c0+Pc1+Pc2*sin. ✓
**Candidate 19 verdict: [MATCH]**
